<div id="review_3561096154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3561096154" />
    <a title="Chiara | _ckarys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53037726-chiara-ckarys"><img alt="Chiara | _ckarys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603892442p2/53037726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3561096154?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chiara | _ckarys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chiara | _ckarys" href="/user/show/53037726-chiara-ckarys">Chiara | _ckarys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53037726-chiara-ckarys?shelf=indie-books">indie-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3561096154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer818722461322644018"><i>I was gifted an ebook copy by the author to review.</i><br/><br/><b>Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>The Threat Below</i> is the first book in a YA post-apocalyptic fantasy series in which humanity has migrated on top of a mountain village to escape extinction by the hands of humanoid monsters from “Down Below”.<br/><br/>Given the author’s screenwriting background, it comes as no surprise that this book was as engaging and heart-stopping as a fantasy or dystopian movie! There was action and mystery around every corner, which is especially en</span>
  <span id="freeText818722461322644018" style="display:none"><i>I was gifted an ebook copy by the author to review.</i><br /><br /><b>Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>The Threat Below</i> is the first book in a YA post-apocalyptic fantasy series in which humanity has migrated on top of a mountain village to escape extinction by the hands of humanoid monsters from “Down Below”.<br /><br />Given the author’s screenwriting background, it comes as no surprise that this book was as engaging and heart-stopping as a fantasy or dystopian movie! There was action and mystery around every corner, which is especially enjoyable given the size of this chunky book. Every chapter seemed to end in a cliffhanger, which kept me hooked. The writing style was easy to follow and entertaining, though it took some getting used to the shifts in perspectives (Icelyn’s chapters are told in first person, while the others are in third person).<br /><br />The aspect that fascinated me most of all was the world-building. The narration moves between the world of Mountaintop (the human village on the mountain) and that of Down Below, home of the Threat Belows who have caused the near-extinction of humanity. Every aspect of both of these worlds is fleshed out in minute detail. The references to the world as we know it, with technologies that are a thing of the past in this world, was a treat, as it was fascinating to see how humanity’s mindset seemed to have taken a step back in terms of mentalities, traditions and beliefs. At the same time, I loved learning more of the Threat Belows—how they came to be, the origins of their history of violence and their motivations moving forward. I liked to call them my Post-Apocalyptic Gollums, and just like the famous character in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> franchise, I alternated between feeling sorry for the pain they went through, feeling affection for their child-like naiveté and being terrified of their violent outbursts.<br /><br />The one aspect I would have liked more of were the characters, toward whom I have conflicting feelings. On the one hand, the immaturity of the main characters, Icelyn, Adorane and Torrain, was justifiable by their age, which actually is a merit to the author for the realistic representation. However, I struggled to believe in the volatility of their emotions toward one another and I had difficulty understanding Icelyn’s god complex in relation to the Threat Belows. I also would have liked a more prominent, mature adult presence in the book to balance things out.<br /><br />Overall, I recommend this book to lovers of fantasy and dystopian novels rich with intrigue and action, along the lines of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> and <i>The Hunger Games</i>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="818722461322644018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3526206784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3526206784" />
    <a title="Maria Elena | _mkarys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53037734-maria-elena-mkarys"><img alt="Maria Elena | _mkarys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603893857p2/53037734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3526206784?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Elena | _mkarys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Elena | _mkarys" href="/user/show/53037734-maria-elena-mkarys">Maria Elena | _mkarys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53037734-maria-elena-mkarys?shelf=indie-authors">indie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53037734-maria-elena-mkarys?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53037734-maria-elena-mkarys?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3526206784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer683811316431581862"><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>The Threat Below</i> is the first book in the Brathius History series. It is set in a post-apocalyptic version of our world three hundred years in the future. <br/><br/>What I enjoyed most of this book was the incredible world-building. The survivors of the human race live on top of the Mountain, where a rigid social structure is set in place. There is the elite intellectual class of the Cognates, and the worker class known as Veritas. The author did a wonderful job at showing the diff</span>
  <span id="freeText683811316431581862" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>The Threat Below</i> is the first book in the Brathius History series. It is set in a post-apocalyptic version of our world three hundred years in the future. <br /><br />What I enjoyed most of this book was the incredible world-building. The survivors of the human race live on top of the Mountain, where a rigid social structure is set in place. There is the elite intellectual class of the Cognates, and the worker class known as Veritas. The author did a wonderful job at showing the differences between the classes, and the deep-rooted prejudices and bigotry of the Cognates toward the Veritas, who they deem to be lesser. This rigidness atop the Mountain is brutal, for anyone who doesn’t fit the established canons deemed worthy by the Cognates is exiled to live the rest of their lives Below, where living—or better yet, surviving is difficult because of the monsters that plague the land, the Threat Below. <br /><br />There was a lot of information to process in the first part of the book. The story got a lot more interesting the moment the civilization on the Mountain discover the water supply is being poisoned. An expedition is formed and the protagonist, Icelyn, sneaks down with them despite her father’s wishes to remain home, where it’s safe. The moment Icelyn travels down the mountain, we discover more about these monsters terrorizing the humans and the history of the world. <br /><br />Among the characters, I preferred Adorane most of all. Adorane is a Veritas, but despite this he is Icelyn’s best friend. Between him and Torrain, Icelyn’s intended, he is the one who questions the girl most often, trying to make her see reason even when her good intentions could lead to a potential disaster. Torrain, on the other hand, often succumbs to Icelyn’s whims, as if he can’t truly make up his mind on his own. As for Icelyn, she wasn’t always easy to like for she often appeared to be very self-absorbed.<br /><br />I did have an issue with the writing style. There were moments the narrative is in third person, others were it was in first person. This sudden switch threw me off and was difficult to follow sometimes. While I adore books with multiple perspectives, this is the first time I’ve seen an author adopt this writing style. <br /><br />I recommend this book to lovers of fantasies such as <i>Lord of the Rings</i> and dystopians like <i>The Hunger Games</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="683811316431581862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15508207283102274128">Thank you to the author for providing me with a copy of The Threat Below in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>I DNF’d this book at 40% though I tried not to, it’s just not working for me.<br/><br/>The narrative was off-putting as it jumps from first person to third person all throughout the chapters that I’ve finished. I like multiple POVs, however, this was poorly executed. The POV keeps on changing that makes it so confusing.   <span id="freeText15508207283102274128" style="display:none">Thank you to the author for providing me with a copy of The Threat Below in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />I DNF’d this book at 40% though I tried not to, it’s just not working for me.<br /><br />The narrative was off-putting as it jumps from first person to third person all throughout the chapters that I’ve finished. I like multiple POVs, however, this was poorly executed. The POV keeps on changing that makes it so confusing. In most chapters, POV changed multiple times within a single chapter.<br /><br />The characters are not likeable enough. I don’t like stupid characters and this book has a few of them. I don’t recall the characters being described properly hence I can’t even picture them in my head. Did I miss that part?<br /><br />Timeline and pacing is also off, while other scenes take weeks, the next scene could be as quick as few minutes. Also, there’s a lot of parentheses, I understand that an explanation is needed but I wished it was executed better.<br /><br />The idea is interesting although I’ve seen similarity with the film Smallfoot by Warner Bros. Who came up with the idea first? I have no answer to that but what I know is this book is not for me.</span>

<div id="review_1434627239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1434627239" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11604542-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1434627239?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/11604542-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/26173407-the-threat-below">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1434627239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6664044319991080662">So everyone seems to love this book... and while the story is good there I had some serious issues with this book including how its written, the characters and plot holes/discrepancies. <br/><br/>The characters live by a strict and oddly inconsistent "Code" - which once the backstory of the founder of their community is revealed, becomes even more confusing because nothing is really provided to explain what the Code was designed to actually accomplish or why the rules are laid out as they are.<br/><br/>The narratio</span>
  <span id="freeText6664044319991080662" style="display:none">So everyone seems to love this book... and while the story is good there I had some serious issues with this book including how its written, the characters and plot holes/discrepancies. <br /><br />The characters live by a strict and oddly inconsistent "Code" - which once the backstory of the founder of their community is revealed, becomes even more confusing because nothing is really provided to explain what the Code was designed to actually accomplish or why the rules are laid out as they are.<br /><br />The narration/point of view is a bit of a mess, changing mid-chapter, or even after a paragraph, with no rhyme or reason or cue to the reader.<br /><br />Technology is an interesting problem, where 300+ year old items seem to magically appear/be found in mostly working order and characters who would have no idea what said objects are (or do they? the descriptions of the education the characters receive varies wildly) can instantly identify, repair, and use them.<br /><br />The passage of time is unclear - parts that happen in a day result in the character aging up, even in appearance, and then in other points of view, the passage of a day is treated like a month.<br /><br />Additionally the main character's thoughts, beliefs, and behavior don't match yet the only cognitive dissonance she seems to suffer is related to her personal relationships.<br /><br />I think this story could actually make a really good TV show - but in order for it to be successful as a novel, it needs some work and a good editorial team.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6664044319991080662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1720391388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720391388" />
    <a title="Midu Hadi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2260566-midu-hadi"><img alt="Midu Hadi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443345786p2/2260566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720391388?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Midu Hadi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Midu Hadi" href="/user/show/2260566-midu-hadi">Midu Hadi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26011212-the-threat-below">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=500-pager">500-pager</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=read-in-september">read-in-september</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=first-in-the-series">first-in-the-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=failed-experiments">failed-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2260566-midu-hadi?shelf=gender-roles">gender-roles</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1720391388&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720391388" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2409467093094239762"><br/>I won this book in a giveaway and the author, Jason Latshaw, was kind enough to send the 500-paged book all the way to Pakistan. This is why, I started scribbling on the book when I started to read it, so that I did it justice.<br/><br/>The first annotation that I added:<br/><br/>Ten pages in and discrimination has already raised its ugly head!<br/><br/>The only people who survive the disaster that kills everybody else are now living on top of a mountain since the rest of the world has turned hostile. Among them, the Cognate</span>
  <span id="freeText2409467093094239762" style="display:none"><br>I won this book in a giveaway and the author, Jason Latshaw, was kind enough to send the 500-paged book all the way to Pakistan. This is why, I started scribbling on the book when I started to read it, so that I did it justice.<br><br>The first annotation that I added:<br><br>Ten pages in and discrimination has already raised its ugly head!<br><br>The only people who survive the disaster that kills everybody else are now living on top of a mountain since the rest of the world has turned hostile. Among them, the Cognates are the thinkers and thus more superior to the Veritas who are doers. The discriminatory status is quite clear right from the start. It is also very much a part of the female protagonist, Icelyn. She may have feelings for a boy who belongs to the class of Veritas but the discrimination is so deeply ingrained that it is plain to see.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472880559i/20337671._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472880625i/20337698._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>An Example<br><br>Which brings me to Icelyn's character. She is self-absorbed to such an extreme that you keep thinking she couldn't possibly be any more so. You'd be wrong! That's because the girl who already has a god complex discovers a whole sect of creatures who worship her! I could go on and on about her character flaws. Instead, I will let this highly useful <a href="http://hannahheath-writer.blogspot.com/2016/07/writing-teenage-characters-what-youre.html" rel="nofollow noopener">post</a> do it for me. It talks about how NOT to write teenage characters.<br><br>Icelyn was not a very likeable person. She discriminated, had a superiority complex, and vacillated between feeling a child who needs her parents to protect her at certain times and takes over the Mountain and kicks her father off the throne. But most of all, she was a master manipulator. She was as good as her ancestor, who had created the monsters, had been at manipulation. She could make them believe that she loved them and then order them to their deaths! Even with all that, there is no character growth when it comes to Icelyn.<br><br>The second thing I noticed was the author's penchant for adding details in parentheses. So many of these details came off as afterthoughts that they might have added during editing. It sounded like they wanted to explain away any doubts the reader have about the story.<br><br>On the other hand, certain things that require explanation are lacking it. Adorane using squirrels to send messages inscribed on nuts is one instance. Where did he learn to do that? How did he train the squirrels? Why are we just hearing of this? Why is it never mentioned again?<br><br>It was then while reading seventh chapter that I got to the biggest issue that I had with the book: jumping points of view (PoVs). They jump enough to give you whiplash. You had to keep guessing which character is doing the talking!<br><br>In case, you have started to think that this book is not for you, these beautiful pieces of writing from it might change your mind:<br><br>"I could even live in the Lost Labyrinth -- the vast unmapped mines that the Kith dug over the centuries, endlessly searching for metals and minerals. They could use a good haunting, and I could be a lost soul aimlessly wandering."<br><br>"On the western side of our Mountain, a giant stretch of blue -- the ocean!-- goes on as far as I can see. This water's alive and angry in places, rising up and slapping the land where they meet, and then retreating to gather energy and do it again. Where the shore and water collide, waves explode into pure white, bursting into the sky like a celebration."<br><br>"Fear is the most elegant weapon Your hands are never messy, Threatening bodily harm is crude. Work, instead on minds and beliefs, play insecurities like a piano. Be creative in approach. Force anxiety to excruciating levels or gently undermine the public confidence. Panic drives herds over cliffs. When nothing is safe, sacred, or sane, there is no respite from horror. Absolutes are quicksilver. Results are spectacular."<br><br>"If I invented a god, he would carry a flare or a lamp or something more magical than a hammer. I wonder, does Ad's god tote a hammer, or some other tool? Maybe a mixer or a chopper. Never know when a god might need to mix or chop something."<br><br>"No! They were machines. They had engines that drew energy from a liquid called gasoline. Believe or not, gasoline was the liquefied remains of monsters who has died millions of years ago, called Dinosaurs." Yeah, may be just a tad exaggerated but fun to read. How would we describe our technology to someone from the past (or a post-apocalyptic future)? Would they even believe us or act like Icelyn did:<br><br>"Machines drinking the liquefied corpses of giant lizards so that they can carry people around inside, as if they're grand wheelbarrows come alive? What ever could be considered fanciful about that?"<br><br>I think I found an allusion to The Hobbit in the book. Icelyn compares the many colored fishes to treasure in this words: (Apriori are the people who had been alive before the disaster took place.)<br><br>"Belubus uses to read an ancient book to me, written for Apriori children, about a great hidden treasure guarded by a giant dragon."<br><br>Another thing that I wanted to share was a scene that stayed with me. It described what happened after the monsters who had brought about the apocalypse had killed for the first time. They ate the woman's (Shai's) flesh and then:<br><br>"Amp hangs the husk of Shai on the wall, from a hook where Mister Sean would often place his coats."<br><br>After reading the description of the monsters or Threatbelows, I imagined they would look like this:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472880736i/20337743.jpg" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Amp would be different and look like this guy:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472880811i/20337746.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This is how I imagined Omathius would be:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472880870i/20337749.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>All of them had sharp claws and Icelyn's ice blue eyes:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472880911i/20337787.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>There are cute illustrations at the beginning of each chapter that tell you where the events are taking place:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472880944i/20337796.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> I was reading the reviews for the book on Goodreads and found an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1434627239?book_show_action=true" rel="nofollow noopener">opinion</a> that I completely agree with. It also sums my review beautifully:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472881016i/20338460.png" width="400" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Also reviewed at:</b><br><a href="&lt;br%20/&gt;http://miduhadi.booklikes.com/post/1461224/what-happens-if-a-teenager-with-a-god-complex-has-an-army-that-worships-her-the-threat-below-by-jason-latshaw-shows-you" rel="nofollow noopener">BL</a><br><a href="http://midureads.blogspot.com/2016/09/what-happens-if-teenager-with-god.html" rel="nofollow noopener">BS</a><br><a href="https://midureads.wordpress.com/2016/09/03/what-happens-if-a-teenager-with-a-god-complex-has-an-army-that-worships-her-the-threat-below-by-jason-latshaw-shows-you/" rel="nofollow noopener">WP</a><br><a href="https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/what-happens-teenager-god-complex-has-army-worships-her-midu-hadi?trk=hp-feed-article-title-publish" rel="nofollow noopener">LI</a></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oBO/oydXMfTJmD8bdlqTFe38YVkS85s2+nLjF0YFTiqp9k7fNT3Eamr2IojuIXTh5mDIVPUAb3xEZb0OffwWEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('piG2jmlg6M4J3EZPkH08jHgVIaYOoqjpsYMerPdUAlyvxEfyewodUKqyW9wIBtt4c4mIq+lRXKMPlEC1zK1aZw==')})
  }

Unfortunately, Madison suffers from prosopagnosia—face blindness—so even though she had a clear view of the murder, she can’t describe the victim or the killer. With no forensic evidence that a crime was committed and no description of the victim to match to a body, the police have no choice but to close the file.  But Shaye Archer doesn’t have the same limitations.  When Shaye hears Madison’s story, she believes the young woman saw exactly what she claims, and even though Shaye knows finding the killer will be next to impossible, she can’t turn down the distraught woman.
